File: /ai-inventor/aii_data/runs/run_ITc1Qruy7fap/3_invention_loop/iter_1/gen_art/gen_art_research_1/research_report.md

# Research Report: SBFL, Pyswip, NL-to-FOL Pipelines, and Benchmark Survey

## 1. Ochiai Formula and Stratified Coverage

### Exact Ochiai Formula

The Ochiai formula for computing suspiciousness scores in Spectrum-Based Fault Localization (SBFL) is:

```
Ochiai(s) = ef(s) / sqrt((ef(s) + nf(s)) * (ef(s) + ep(s)))
```

**Variable definitions:**
- `ef` (executed by failing): number of **failed** test cases that execute (cover) element `s`
- `nf` (not executed by failing): number of **failed** test cases that do NOT execute element `s`
- `ep` (executed by passing): number of **passed** test cases that execute element `s`
- `np` (not executed by passing): number of **passed** test cases that do NOT execute element `s`

**Note:** `np` is **not used** in Ochiai (unlike Tarantula). The score range is `[0, 1]`, where 1 = maximum suspicion (element only appears in failed tests). The Ochiai formula rewards elements with high `ef` and penalizes elements also covered by passing tests (high `ep`).

**Tarantula formula for comparison:**
```
Tarantula(s) = (ef/totalfailed) / ((ef/totalfailed) + (ep/totalpassed))
```

**Tie-breaking:** Standard practice is to use statement/predicate order or random ordering when scores are equal.

### Mapping to Prolog Predicate Coverage

In the Prolog-SLD resolution context:
- **Program element** = predicate clause (predicate name/arity)
- **Test case** = oracle query (NL premise set + NL conclusion)
- **Test pass** = Prolog proof succeeds (answer matches ground truth label)
- **Test fail** = Prolog proof fails or returns wrong answer

Coverage matrix mapping:
- `ef` = failed queries where predicate was accessed (called or unified) during SLD resolution
- `ep` = passing queries where predicate was accessed
- `nf` = failed queries where predicate was NOT accessed at all

### Stratified Coverage Design

Standard SBFL uses binary coverage (accessed / not accessed). For Prolog, a **stratified** coverage distinguishes:

1. **Direct unification failure**: `call` port fires, `unify` port does NOT fire → clause head does not match the goal term
2. **Indirect (sub-goal) failure**: `unify` port fires (head matched successfully), but `exit` port does NOT fire and `fail` fires → head matched but sub-goals failed downstream
3. **Success**: both `unify` and `exit` fire

This stratification creates a 4-column spectrum per predicate: direct-fail count, indirect-fail count, success-on-fail-query count, success-on-pass-query count. The Ochiai formula can still be applied, but the most direct signal for a KB error is a predicate that has direct unification failures concentrated in failed queries.

---

## 2. SWI-Prolog / Pyswip Tracing for SLD Coverage

### Recommended Approach: Meta-Interpreter (Option B)

For instrumentation via pyswip, the **recommended approach** is a pure Prolog meta-interpreter (vanilla interpreter pattern) rather than the tracer hook system. Reasons:
- More portable — does not depend on SWI-Prolog trace hook internals
- Can be loaded via `consult()` from Python and queried via `Prolog.query()`
- No need to arm/disarm the debugger from Python
- Outcomes recorded in a Prolog global list, extractable to Python via `query()`

### The Trace Hook API (Option A — for reference)

The exact predicate signature is:
```prolog
prolog_trace_interception(+Port, +Frame, +Choice, -Action)
```

- **Port**: one of `call`, `redo(PC)`, `unify`, `exit`, `fail`, `exception(Except)`, `cut_call(PC)`, `cut_exit(PC)`
- **Frame**: integer reference to the current local stack frame
- **Choice**: reference to the last choice point
- **Action**: must be unified with one of: `abort`, `halt`, `continue` (creep — no interference), `fail`, `ignore`, `nodebug`, `leap`, `retry`, `skip`, `up`

**To continue without interference, return `continue`.**

```prolog
prolog_trace_interception(Port, Frame, _PC, continue) :-
    prolog_frame_attribute(Frame, goal, Goal),
    prolog_frame_attribute(Frame, level, Level),
    recordz(trace, trace(Port, Level, Goal)).
```

**Key frame attributes via `prolog_frame_attribute/3`:**
- `goal`: the goal term associated with the frame (gives functor name and arity)
- `level`: recursion depth of the frame (top-level = 0)
- `predicate_indicator`: `<module>:<name>/<arity>` — avoids creating illegal terms
- `clause`: reference to the currently running clause
- `parent`: reference to parent stack frame

### Ports for Stratified Coverage

| Port | Meaning for Stratification |
|------|---------------------------|
| `call` | Predicate invoked — SLD resolution begins |
| `unify` | Neck instruction — head matching succeeded |
| `exit` | Goal proved — all subgoals succeeded |
| `fail` | Final failure — predicate could not prove goal |

**Detection logic:**
- `call` fires → `unify` does NOT fire: **direct unification failure** (clause head doesn't match)
- `unify` fires → `exit` does NOT fire (then `fail` fires): **indirect / sub-goal failure**
- `unify` fires → `exit` fires: **success**

### Meta-Interpreter Pattern for Outcome Recording

```prolog
:- dynamic coverage/3.  % coverage(PredicateName/Arity, Event, QueryId)

% Instrumented meta-interpreter
prove(true, _QueryId) :- !.
prove((A, B), QueryId) :- !,
    prove(A, QueryId),
    prove(B, QueryId).
prove(Goal, QueryId) :-
    functor(Goal, Name, Arity),
    functor(Head, Name, Arity),
    clause(Head, Body),
    % Record successful unification
    assertz(coverage(Name/Arity, unified, QueryId)),
    Goal = Head,
    ( prove(Body, QueryId) ->
        assertz(coverage(Name/Arity, exit, QueryId))
    ;
        assertz(coverage(Name/Arity, subgoal_fail, QueryId)),
        fail
    ).
prove(Goal, QueryId) :-
    functor(Goal, Name, Arity),
    \+ clause(Goal, _),
    assertz(coverage(Name/Arity, direct_fail, QueryId)),
    fail.

% Run a query and collect coverage
run_query(Goal, QueryId, Result) :-
    ( prove(Goal, QueryId) ->
        Result = proved
    ;
        Result = failed
    ).
```

**Integration via pyswip:**
```python
from pyswip import Prolog
prolog = Prolog()
prolog.consult('kb.pl')         # load the knowledge base
prolog.consult('meta_interp.pl')  # load the meta-interpreter
# Run query and collect coverage
list(prolog.query('run_query(conclusion_goal, q1, Result)'))
# Extract coverage events
coverage = list(prolog.query('coverage(Pred, Event, QueryId)'))
```

---

## 3. Logic-LM Prompting Format

### Architecture

Logic-LM uses a three-stage pipeline:
1. **Problem Formulator**: LLM translates NL problem into task-specific symbolic language (few-shot)
2. **Symbolic Reasoner**: deterministic solver (Pyke for LP, Prover9 for FOL, python-constraint for CSP, SAT solver for AR)
3. **Result Interpreter**: maps symbolic answer back to NL

### Few-Shot Prompt Structure

Logic-LM uses **two different symbolic formats** for different dataset types:

**FOLIO (First-Order Logic) format:**
```
Given a problem description and a question. The task is to parse the problem 
and the question into first-order logic formulars. The grammar of the 
first-order logic formular is defined as follows:
1) logical conjunction of expr1 and expr2: expr1 ∧ expr2
2) logical disjunction of expr1 and expr2: expr1 ∨ expr2
3) logical exclusive disjunction of expr1 and expr2: expr1 ⊕ expr2
4) logical negation of expr1: ¬expr1
5) expr1 implies expr2: expr1 → expr2
6) expr1 if and only if expr2: expr1 ↔ expr2
7) logical universal quantification: ∀x
8) logical existential quantification: ∃x
------
Problem: [NL problem text]
Question: [NL question text]
### Predicates:
PredicateName(x) ::: English description of x
...
Premises:
∀x (P(x) → Q(x)) ::: English NL sentence
...
Conclusion:
P(entity) ::: English NL conclusion sentence
------
Problem: [[PROBLEM]]
Question: [[QUESTION]]
###
```

**ProofWriter (Logic Programming) format:**
```
Task Description: You are given a problem description and a question. The task is to:
1) define all the predicates in the problem
2) parse the problem into logic rules based on the defined predicates
3) write all the facts mentioned in the problem
4) parse the question into the logic form
------
Problem: [NL problem]
Question: [NL question]
### Predicates:
Predicate($x, bool) ::: Is x predicate?
Facts:
Predicate(Entity, True) ::: English NL sentence
Rules:
Predicate1($x, True) && Predicate2($x, True) >>> Predicate3($x, True) ::: English rule
Query:
Predicate(Entity, True) ::: English conclusion
------
Problem: [[PROBLEM]]
Question: [[QUESTION]]
###
```

### Predicate Naming Conventions

- **FOLIO/FOL format**: CamelCase predicates (e.g., `ChoralConductor(x)`, `Dependent(x)`, `Love(x,y)`)
- **ProofWriter/LP format**: CamelCase predicates with bool parameter (e.g., `Quiet($x, bool)`, `Young($x, bool)`)
- Constants: lowercase atoms (e.g., `miroslav`, `rina`, `anne`) or `year1946` for years
- Variables: `x`, `y`, `z` or `$x` in LP format
- Comments/descriptions: triple colon `:::` separator for English gloss

### Self-Refinement Feedback Format

Logic-LM feeds solver **error messages** back to the LLM:
```
You gave me this [erroneous logic form].
The solver returned error: [error message]
Common errors and remedies:
- [example error] → [remedy]
```
Runs iteratively until no error messages returned OR maximum revisions reached.

---

## 4. FOLIO Benchmark Protocol

### Dataset Structure

| Property | Value |
|----------|-------|
| Total examples | 1,435 conclusions from 487 story sets |
| Train split | 1,001 examples |
| Validation split | 203 examples |
| Test split | 226 examples (labels not publicly released) |
| Labels | True / False / Unknown |
| Data format | JSONL |

**JSONL fields per example:**
- `story_id`: unique story identifier
- `premises`: list of NL sentences
- `conclusion`: NL conclusion sentence
- `label`: True / False / Unknown
- `premises-FOL`: list of FOL formulas (parallel to premises)
- `conclusion-FOL`: FOL formula for conclusion

### Evaluation Metrics

**For logical reasoning task:**
- **Accuracy**: correct prediction of True/False/Unknown label

**For NL-FOL translation task:**
- **SynV (Syntactic Validity)**: binary score — is the generated FOL formula parseable by the inference engine? (GPT-4 achieves ~93.9% with few-shot)
- **EAcc (Execution Accuracy)**: does running the generated FOL through the inference engine produce the correct truth value label? (GPT-4 achieves ~63.8% with few-shot — much harder)

### Inference Engine

FOLIO uses a custom **FOL inference engine** based on standard FOL prover to verify FOL annotations during construction (details in Appendix G of the paper). For EAcc evaluation, the generated FOL is executed through this engine to check if it produces the correct True/False/Unknown answer.

### Label Distribution

Not perfectly balanced — FOLIO has more "True" labels than "False" or "Unknown" (models tend to predict "True" more frequently, as noted in the paper's error analysis). The WikiLogic subset (304 stories) and HybLogic subset (183 stories) have different logical patterns.

### Standard Evaluation Protocol

LINC uses the validation set (182 examples after removing 22 with errors) for evaluation. Logic-LM typically evaluates on the validation set. No fixed test set evaluation protocol has been established (test labels not released as of the 2022 paper).

---

## 5. ProofWriter Benchmark Protocol

### Dataset Variants

| Variant | Reasoning Depth | Notes |
|---------|----------------|-------|
| D0 | 0 hops (trivial) | Direct fact lookup |
| D1 | ≤1 hop | Single rule application |
| D2 | ≤2 hops | Two-step reasoning |
| D3 | ≤3 hops | Three-step reasoning |
| D5 | ≤5 hops | Longest chains |

Each D* dataset contains **100k questions**.

### World Assumption Variants

- **CWA (Closed-World Assumption)**: Labels are True/False only (negation-as-failure)
- **OWA (Open-World Assumption)**: Labels are True/False/Unknown (explicit unknowns allowed)

The OWA version is **recommended** for comparison with FOLIO since it matches the three-label schema. Logic-LM and LINC both use the OWA version.

### Natural Language Surface Form

ProofWriter uses **templated natural language** (e.g., "Anne is quiet. If someone is quiet then they are red."). The "ParaRules" variant uses crowdworker-paraphrased text that is more naturalistic. Logic-LM uses the standard OWA version and acknowledges the templatic text limitation.

### Recommended Evaluation Subset

**Logic-LM protocol**: OWA depth-5 subset, **600 examples** randomly sampled from test set with balanced label distribution (200 each of PROVED/DISPROVED/UNKNOWN).

**LINC protocol**: OWA version, **360 balanced samples** — 50 per depth (0-5), 120 per label (True/False/Uncertain), 20 per depth×label combination.

### Data Format Fields

Each example contains:
- `theory`: list of NL sentences (facts + rules)
- `question`: NL conclusion to evaluate
- `answer`: True/False/Unknown (or PROVED/DISPROVED/UNKNOWN)
- `proof`: structured proof tree with intermediate steps and supporting facts/rules

### Negation-as-Failure and Prolog

Under CWA, Prolog's built-in `\+` (negation as failure) maps cleanly to the ProofWriter semantics. Under OWA, a three-way classifier is needed — Prolog `\+` would erroneously treat "unknown" facts as false.

---

## 6. Baseline Comparison Framework

### Self-Refine Baseline

**Three-component structure:**
1. `pgen` (initial generation prompt): few-shot examples of input→output
2. `pfb` (feedback prompt): few-shot examples of input+output→feedback; feedback is an NL critique identifying concrete phrases to change
3. `prefine` (refinement prompt): full history x, y0, fb0, ..., yt, fbt → refined output yt+1

**Algorithm:**
```
y0 = M(pgen || x)
for t in 0, 1, ...:
    fb_t = M(pfb || x || y_t)
    if stop(fb_t, t): break
    y_{t+1} = M(prefine || x || y0 || fb0 || ... || y_t || fb_t)
return y_t
```

**Stopping conditions**: fixed max iterations OR model signals "this output is satisfactory."

**Key differentiator from SBFL**: Self-Refine gives **global NL critique** of the entire KB (e.g., "Query Q fails because predicate P is defined incorrectly"). It does NOT produce ranked suspiciousness scores per predicate. The SBFL pipeline provides a **ranked list of suspicious predicates with numeric scores**, enabling targeted revision rather than holistic re-generation.

### LINC Baseline

**Translation approach**: Few-shot (8 in-context examples from FOLIO training set for both FOLIO and ProofWriter). Prompts each premise and conclusion with XML-style `<PREMISE>`/`<CONCLUSION>` tags.

**Representation**: Prover9 FOL syntax — NOT Prolog LP syntax
- Variables: lowercase `x`, `y`
- Universal quantification: `all x. (predicate(x) -> predicate2(x))`
- Existential quantification: `exists x. (predicate(x))`
- Connectives: `->`, `&`, `|`, `-` (negation)

**Theorem prover**: Prover9 (external FOL prover, NOT SWI-Prolog)

**Failure modes without feedback:**
- L1: FOL misses implicit commonsense not stated in premises
- L2: Natural language nuance cannot be captured in first-order logic
- L3: Predicate naming inconsistencies across premises

**Datasets**: FOLIO validation (182 cleaned examples) and ProofWriter OWA (360 balanced samples)

### Logic-LM Baseline

**Translation approach**: Few-shot (dataset-specific — 2+ examples per dataset)

**Representation**: Dataset-specific — FOL for FOLIO (Prover9), LP for ProofWriter (Pyke engine)

**Self-refinement**: Uses solver error messages as structured feedback (not NL critique)

**ProofWriter accuracy by depth** (Logic-LM paper, Figure 3):
- D0: ~81.7% (Logic-LM) vs ~73.6% (CoT) vs ~76.3% (Standard)
- D5: ~71.1% (Logic-LM) vs ~51.0% (CoT) vs ~33.5% (Standard)
Logic-LM advantage grows with reasoning depth.

### Structural Differences from Dual-Signal SBFL Pipeline

| Dimension | Self-Refine | LINC | Logic-LM | Proposed SBFL Pipeline |
|-----------|------------|------|----------|----------------------|
| Feedback signal | Global NL critique | None (one-shot) | Solver error message | Ranked per-predicate suspiciousness scores |
| Feedback granularity | Whole KB | N/A | Per-formula syntax error | Per predicate, with stratification |
| Revision targeting | Holistic re-generation | N/A | Specific erroneous clause | Highest-suspicion predicate first |
| Debugging information | Which queries failed | N/A | What syntax is wrong | Which predicates correlate with failures |
| Iterative strategy | Random walk through NL space | N/A | Fix syntax errors only | Guided search using SBFL ranking |

**For fair comparison**: All systems should receive the same NL-to-Prolog initial translation (same LLM, same few-shot examples), same oracle queries, and same number of revision iterations. The SBFL pipeline is compared on final KB accuracy (EAcc), not intermediate metrics.
````

### [90] TOOL RESULT — Write · 2026-06-07 05:03:32 UTC

{"type": "create", "filePath": "/ai-inventor/aii_data/runs/run_ITc1Qruy7fap/3_invention_loop/iter_1/gen_art/gen_art_research_1/research_report.md", "content": "# Research Report: SBFL, Pyswip, NL-to-FOL Pipelines, and Benchmark Survey\n\n## 1. Ochiai Formula and Stratified Coverage\n\n### Exact Ochiai Formula\n\nThe Ochiai formula for computing suspiciousness scores in Spectrum-Based Fault Localization (SBFL) is:\n\n```\nOchiai(s) = ef(s) / sqrt((ef(s) + nf(s)) * (ef(s) + ep(s)))\n```\n\n**Variable definitions:**\n- `ef` (executed by failing): number of **failed** test cases that execute (cover) element `s`\n- `nf` (not executed by failing): number of **failed** test cases that do NOT execute element `s`\n- `ep` (executed by passing): number of **passed** test cases that execute element `s`\n- `np` (not executed by passing): number of **passed** test cases that do NOT execute element `s`\n\n**Note:** `np` is **not used** in Ochiai (unlike Tarantula). The score range is `[0, 1]`, where 1 = maximum suspicion (element only appears in failed tests). The Ochiai formula rewards elements with high `ef` and penalizes elements also covered by passing tests (high `ep`).\n\n**Tarantula formula for comparison:**\n```\nTarantula(s) = (ef/totalfailed) / ((ef/totalfailed) + (ep/totalpassed))\n```\n\n**Tie-breaking:** Standard practice is to use statement/predicate order or random ordering when scores are equal.\n\n### Mapping to Prolog Predicate Coverage\n\nIn the Prolog-SLD resolution context:\n- **Program element** = predicate clause (predicate name/arity)\n- **Test case** = oracle query (NL premise set + NL conclusion)\n- **Test pass** = Prolog proof succeeds (answer matches ground truth label)\n- **Test fail** = Prolog proof fails or returns wrong answer\n\nCoverage matrix mapping:\n- `ef` = failed queries where predicate was accessed (called or unified) during SLD resolution\n- `ep` = passing queries where predicate was accessed\n- `nf` = failed queries where predicate was NOT accessed at all\n\n### Stratified Coverage Design\n\nStandard SBFL uses binary coverage (accessed / not accessed). For Prolog, a **stratified** coverage distinguishes:\n\n1. **Direct unification failure**: `call` port fires, `unify` port does NOT fire → clause head does not match the goal term\n2. **Indirect (sub-goal) failure**: `unify` port fires (head matched successfully), but `exit` port does NOT fire and `fail` fires → head matched but sub-goals failed downstream\n3. **Success**: both `unify` and `exit` fire\n\nThis stratification creates a 4-column spectrum per predicate: direct-fail count, indirect-fail count, success-on-fail-query count, success-on-pass-query count. The Ochiai formula can still be applied, but the most direct signal for a KB error is a predicate that has direct unification failures concentrated in failed queries.\n\n---\n\n## 2. SWI-Prolog / Pyswip Tracing for SLD Coverage\n\n### Recommended Approach: Meta-Interpreter (Option B)\n\nFor instrumentation via pyswip, the **recommended approach** is a pure Prolog meta-interpreter (vanilla interpreter pattern) rather than the tracer hook system. Reasons:\n- More portable — does not depend on SWI-Prolog trace hook internals\n- Can be loaded via `consult()` from Python and queried via `Prolog.query()`\n- No need to arm/disarm the debugger from Python\n- Outcomes recorded in a Prolog global list, extractable to Python via `query()`\n\n### The Trace Hook API (Option A — for reference)\n\nThe exact predicate signature is:\n```prolog\nprolog_trace_interception(+Port, +Frame, +Choice, -Action)\n```\n\n- **Port**: one of `call`, `redo(PC)`, `unify`, `exit`, `fail`, `exception(Except)`, `cut_call(PC)`, `cut_exit(PC)`\n- **Frame**: integer reference to the current local stack frame\n- **Choice**: reference to the last choice point\n- **Action**: must be unified with one of: `abort`, `halt`, `continue` (creep — no interference), `fail`, `ignore`, `nodebug`, `leap`, `retry`, `skip`, `up`\n\n**To continue without interference, return `continue`.**\n\n```prolog\nprolog_trace_interception(Port, Frame, _PC, continue) :-\n    prolog_frame_attribute(Frame, goal, Goal),\n    prolog_frame_attribute(Frame, level, Level),\n    recordz(trace, trace(Port, Level, Goal)).\n```\n\n**Key frame attributes via `prolog_frame_attribute/3`:**\n- `goal`: the goal term associated with the frame (gives functor name and arity)\n- `level`: recursion depth of the frame (top-level = 0)\n- `predicate_indicator`: `<module>:<name>/<arity>` — avoids creating illegal terms\n- `clause`: reference to the currently running clause\n- `parent`: reference to parent stack frame\n\n### Ports for Stratified Coverage\n\n| Port | Meaning for Stratification |\n|------|---------------------------|\n| `call` | Predicate invoked — SLD resolution begins |\n| `unify` | Neck instruction — head matching succeeded |\n| `exit` | Goal proved — all subgoals succeeded |\n| `fail` | Final failure — predicate could not prove goal |\n\n**Detection logic:**\n- `call` fires → `unify` does NOT fire: **direct unification failure** (clause head doesn't match)\n- `unify` fires → `exit` does NOT fire (then `fail` fires): **indirect / sub-goal failure**\n- `unify` fires → `exit` fires: **success**\n\n### Meta-Interpreter Pattern for Outcome Recording\n\n```prolog\n:- dynamic coverage/3.  % coverage(PredicateName/Arity, Event, QueryId)\n\n% Instrumented meta-interpreter\nprove(true, _QueryId) :- !.\nprove((A, B), QueryId) :- !,\n    prove(A, QueryId),\n    prove(B, QueryId).\nprove(Goal, QueryId) :-\n    functor(Goal, Name, Arity),\n    functor(Head, Name, Arity),\n    clause(Head, Body),\n    % Record successful unification\n    assertz(coverage(Name/Arity, unified, QueryId)),\n    Goal = Head,\n    ( prove(Body, QueryId) ->\n        assertz(coverage(Name/Arity, exit, QueryId))\n    ;\n        assertz(coverage(Name/Arity, subgoal_fail, QueryId)),\n        fail\n    ).\nprove(Goal, QueryId) :-\n    functor(Goal, Name, Arity),\n    \\+ clause(Goal, _),\n    assertz(coverage(Name/Arity, direct_fail, QueryId)),\n    fail.\n\n% Run a query and collect coverage\nrun_query(Goal, QueryId, Result) :-\n    ( prove(Goal, QueryId) ->\n        Result = proved\n    ;\n        Result = failed\n    ).\n```\n\n**Integration via pyswip:**\n```python\nfrom pyswip import Prolog\nprolog = Prolog()\nprolog.consult('kb.pl')         # load the knowledge base\nprolog.consult('meta_interp.pl')  # load the meta-interpreter\n# Run query and collect coverage\nlist(prolog.query('run_query(conclusion_goal, q1, Result)'))\n# Extract coverage events\ncoverage = list(prolog.query('coverage(Pred, Event, QueryId)'))\n```\n\n---\n\n## 3. Logic-LM Prompting Format\n\n### Architecture\n\nLogic-LM uses a three-stage pipeline:\n1. **Problem Formulator**: LLM translates NL problem into task-specific symbolic language (few-shot)\n2. **Symbolic Reasoner**: deterministic solver (Pyke for LP, Prover9 for FOL, python-constraint for CSP, SAT solver for AR)\n3. **Result Interpreter**: maps symbolic answer back to NL\n\n### Few-Shot Prompt Structure\n\nLogic-LM uses **two different symbolic formats** for different dataset types:\n\n**FOLIO (First-Order Logic) format:**\n```\nGiven a problem description and a question. The task is to parse the problem \nand the question into first-order logic formulars. The grammar of the \nfirst-order logic formular is defined as follows:\n1) logical conjunction of expr1 and expr2: expr1 ∧ expr2\n2) logical disjunction of expr1 and expr2: expr1 ∨ expr2\n3) logical exclusive disjunction of expr1 and expr2: expr1 ⊕ expr2\n4) logical negation of expr1: ¬expr1\n5) expr1 implies expr2: expr1 → expr2\n6) expr1 if and only if expr2: expr1 ↔ expr2\n7) logical universal quantification: ∀x\n8) logical existential quantification: ∃x\n------\nProblem: [NL problem text]\nQuestion: [NL question text]\n### Predicates:\nPredicateName(x) ::: English description of x\n...\nPremises:\n∀x (P(x) → Q(x)) ::: English NL sentence\n...\nConclusion:\nP(entity) ::: English NL conclusion sentence\n------\nProblem: [[PROBLEM]]\nQuestion: [[QUESTION]]\n###\n```\n\n**ProofWriter (Logic Programming) format:**\n```\nTask Description: You are given a problem description and a question. The task is to:\n1) define all the predicates in the problem\n2) parse the problem into logic rules based on the defined predicates\n3) write all the facts mentioned in the problem\n4) parse the question into the logic form\n------\nProblem: [NL problem]\nQuestion: [NL question]\n### Predicates:\nPredicate($x, bool) ::: Is x predicate?\nFacts:\nPredicate(Entity, True) ::: English NL sentence\nRules:\nPredicate1($x, True) && Predicate2($x, True) >>> Predicate3($x, True) ::: English rule\nQuery:\nPredicate(Entity, True) ::: English conclusion\n------\nProblem: [[PROBLEM]]\nQuestion: [[QUESTION]]\n###\n```\n\n### Predicate Naming Conventions\n\n- **FOLIO/FOL format**: CamelCase predicates (e.g., `ChoralConductor(x)`, `Dependent(x)`, `Love(x,y)`)\n- **ProofWriter/LP format**: CamelCase predicates with bool parameter (e.g., `Quiet($x, bool)`, `Young($x, bool)`)\n- Constants: lowercase atoms (e.g., `miroslav`, `rina`, `anne`) or `year1946` for years\n- Variables: `x`, `y`, `z` or `$x` in LP format\n- Comments/descriptions: triple colon `:::` separator for English gloss\n\n### Self-Refinement Feedback Format\n\nLogic-LM feeds solver **error messages** back to the LLM:\n```\nYou gave me this [erroneous logic form].\nThe solver returned error: [error message]\nCommon errors and remedies:\n- [example error] → [remedy]\n```\nRuns iteratively until no error messages returned OR maximum revisions reached.\n\n---\n\n## 4. FOLIO Benchmark Protocol\n\n### Dataset Structure\n\n| Property | Value |\n|----------|-------|\n| Total examples | 1,435 conclusions from 487 story sets |\n| Train split | 1,001 examples |\n| Validation split | 203 examples |\n| Test split | 226 examples (labels not publicly released) |\n| Labels | True / False / Unknown |\n| Data format | JSONL |\n\n**JSONL fields per example:**\n- `story_id`: unique story identifier\n- `premises`: list of NL sentences\n- `conclusion`: NL conclusion sentence\n- `label`: True / False / Unknown\n- `premises-FOL`: list of FOL formulas (parallel to premises)\n- `conclusion-FOL`: FOL formula for conclusion\n\n### Evaluation Metrics\n\n**For logical reasoning task:**\n- **Accuracy**: correct prediction of True/False/Unknown label\n\n**For NL-FOL translation task:**\n- **SynV (Syntactic Validity)**: binary score — is the generated FOL formula parseable by the inference engine? (GPT-4 achieves ~93.9% with few-shot)\n- **EAcc (Execution Accuracy)**: does running the generated FOL through the inference engine produce the correct truth value label? (GPT-4 achieves ~63.8% with few-shot — much harder)\n\n### Inference Engine\n\nFOLIO uses a custom **FOL inference engine** based on standard FOL prover to verify FOL annotations during construction (details in Appendix G of the paper). For EAcc evaluation, the generated FOL is executed through this engine to check if it produces the correct True/False/Unknown answer.\n\n### Label Distribution\n\nNot perfectly balanced — FOLIO has more \"True\" labels than \"False\" or \"Unknown\" (models tend to predict \"True\" more frequently, as noted in the paper's error analysis). The WikiLogic subset (304 stories) and HybLogic subset (183 stories) have different logical patterns.\n\n### Standard Evaluation Protocol\n\nLINC uses the validation set (182 examples after removing 22 with errors) for evaluation. Logic-LM typically evaluates on the validation set. No fixed test set evaluation protocol has been established (test labels not released as of the 2022 paper).\n\n---\n\n## 5. ProofWriter Benchmark Protocol\n\n### Dataset Variants\n\n| Variant | Reasoning Depth | Notes |\n|---------|----------------|-------|\n| D0 | 0 hops (trivial) | Direct fact lookup |\n| D1 | ≤1 hop | Single rule application |\n| D2 | ≤2 hops | Two-step reasoning |\n| D3 | ≤3 hops | Three-step reasoning |\n| D5 | ≤5 hops | Longest chains |\n\nEach D* dataset contains **100k questions**.\n\n### World Assumption Variants\n\n- **CWA (Closed-World Assumption)**: Labels are True/False only (negation-as-failure)\n- **OWA (Open-World Assumption)**: Labels are True/False/Unknown (explicit unknowns allowed)\n\nThe OWA version is **recommended** for comparison with FOLIO since it matches the three-label schema. Logic-LM and LINC both use the OWA version.\n\n### Natural Language Surface Form\n\nProofWriter uses **templated natural language** (e.g., \"Anne is quiet. If someone is quiet then they are red.\"). The \"ParaRules\" variant uses crowdworker-paraphrased text that is more naturalistic. Logic-LM uses the standard OWA version and acknowledges the templatic text limitation.\n\n### Recommended Evaluation Subset\n\n**Logic-LM protocol**: OWA depth-5 subset, **600 examples** randomly sampled from test set with balanced label distribution (200 each of PROVED/DISPROVED/UNKNOWN).\n\n**LINC protocol**: OWA version, **360 balanced samples** — 50 per depth (0-5), 120 per label (True/False/Uncertain), 20 per depth×label combination.\n\n### Data Format Fields\n\nEach example contains:\n- `theory`: list of NL sentences (facts + rules)\n- `question`: NL conclusion to evaluate\n- `answer`: True/False/Unknown (or PROVED/DISPROVED/UNKNOWN)\n- `proof`: structured proof tree with intermediate steps and supporting facts/rules\n\n### Negation-as-Failure and Prolog\n\nUnder CWA, Prolog's built-in `\\+` (negation as failure) maps cleanly to the ProofWriter semantics. Under OWA, a three-way classifier is needed — Prolog `\\+` would erroneously treat \"unknown\" facts as false.\n\n---\n\n## 6. Baseline Comparison Framework\n\n### Self-Refine Baseline\n\n**Three-component structure:**\n1. `pgen` (initial generation prompt): few-shot examples of input→output\n2. `pfb` (feedback prompt): few-shot examples of input+output→feedback; feedback is an NL critique identifying concrete phrases to change\n3. `prefine` (refinement prompt): full history x, y0, fb0, ..., yt, fbt → refined output yt+1\n\n**Algorithm:**\n```\ny0 = M(pgen || x)\nfor t in 0, 1, ...:\n    fb_t = M(pfb || x || y_t)\n    if stop(fb_t, t): break\n    y_{t+1} = M(prefine || x || y0 || fb0 || ... || y_t || fb_t)\nreturn y_t\n```\n\n**Stopping conditions**: fixed max iterations OR model signals \"this output is satisfactory.\"\n\n**Key differentiator from SBFL**: Self-Refine gives **global NL critique** of the entire KB (e.g., \"Query Q fails because predicate P is defined incorrectly\"). It does NOT produce ranked suspiciousness scores per predicate. The SBFL pipeline provides a **ranked list of suspicious predicates with numeric scores**, enabling targeted revision rather than holistic re-generation.\n\n### LINC Baseline\n\n**Translation approach**: Few-shot (8 in-context examples from FOLIO training set for both FOLIO and ProofWriter). Prompts each premise and conclusion with XML-style `<PREMISE>`/`<CONCLUSION>` tags.\n\n**Representation**: Prover9 FOL syntax — NOT Prolog LP syntax\n- Variables: lowercase `x`, `y`\n- Universal quantification: `all x. (predicate(x) -> predicate2(x))`\n- Existential quantification: `exists x. (predicate(x))`\n- Connectives: `->`, `&`, `|`, `-` (negation)\n\n**Theorem prover**: Prover9 (external FOL prover, NOT SWI-Prolog)\n\n**Failure modes without feedback:**\n- L1: FOL misses implicit commonsense not stated in premises\n- L2: Natural language nuance cannot be captured in first-order logic\n- L3: Predicate naming inconsistencies across premises\n\n**Datasets**: FOLIO validation (182 cleaned examples) and ProofWriter OWA (360 balanced samples)\n\n### Logic-LM Baseline\n\n**Translation approach**: Few-shot (dataset-specific — 2+ examples per dataset)\n\n**Representation**: Dataset-specific — FOL for FOLIO (Prover9), LP for ProofWriter (Pyke engine)\n\n**Self-refinement**: Uses solver error messages as structured feedback (not NL critique)\n\n**ProofWriter accuracy by depth** (Logic-LM paper, Figure 3):\n- D0: ~81.7% (Logic-LM) vs ~73.6% (CoT) vs ~76.3% (Standard)\n- D5: ~71.1% (Logic-LM) vs ~51.0% (CoT) vs ~33.5% (Standard)\nLogic-LM advantage grows with reasoning depth.\n\n### Structural Differences from Dual-Signal SBFL Pipeline\n\n| Dimension | Self-Refine | LINC | Logic-LM | Proposed SBFL Pipeline |\n|-----------|------------|------|----------|----------------------|\n| Feedback signal | Global NL critique | None (one-shot) | Solver error message | Ranked per-predicate suspiciousness scores |\n| Feedback granularity | Whole KB | N/A | Per-formula syntax error | Per predicate, with stratification |\n| Revision targeting | Holistic re-generation | N/A | Specific erroneous clause | Highest-suspicion predicate first |\n| Debugging information | Which queries failed | N/A | What syntax is wrong | Which predicates correlate with failures |\n| Iterative strategy | Random walk through NL space | N/A | Fix syntax errors only | Guided search using SBFL ranking |\n\n**For fair comparison**: All systems should receive the same NL-to-Prolog initial translation (same LLM, same few-shot examples), same oracle queries, and same number of revision iterations. The SBFL pipeline is compared on final KB accuracy (EAcc), not intermediate metrics.\n", "structuredPatch": [], "originalFile": null, "userModified": false}
````

{"type": "create", "filePath": "/ai-inventor/aii_data/runs/run_ITc1Qruy7fap/3_invention_loop/iter_1/gen_art/gen_art_research_1/research_out.json", "content": "{\n  \"answer\": {\n    \"ochiai_formula\": {\n      \"formula\": \"ef / sqrt((ef + nf) * (ef + ep))\",\n      \"variable_definitions\": {\n        \"ef\": \"Number of failed test cases that execute (cover) element s\",\n        \"ep\": \"Number of passing test cases that execute (cover) element s\",\n        \"nf\": \"Number of failed test cases that do NOT execute element s\",\n        \"np\": \"Number of passing test cases that do NOT execute element s — NOT USED in Ochiai (unlike Tarantula)\"\n      },\n      \"range\": \"[0, 1] where 1 = maximum suspicion (element appears only in failed tests)\",\n      \"prolog_mapping\": {\n        \"program_element\": \"predicate clause identified by name/arity\",\n        \"test_case\": \"oracle query (NL premise set + NL conclusion question)\",\n        \"test_pass\": \"Prolog proof succeeds AND matches gold truth label\",\n        \"test_fail\": \"Prolog proof fails or returns wrong truth label\",\n        \"ef\": \"failed oracle queries where predicate was accessed (call or unify port fired) during SLD resolution\",\n        \"ep\": \"passing oracle queries where predicate was accessed\",\n        \"nf\": \"failed oracle queries where predicate was NOT accessed at all\"\n      },\n      \"tarantula_formula_for_comparison\": \"(ef/totalfailed) / ((ef/totalfailed) + (ep/totalpassed))\",\n      \"stratification_approach\": \"SLD resolution produces 4 distinct coverage events per predicate per query: (1) direct_fail: call fires, unify does NOT fire — head does not match; (2) subgoal_fail: unify fires, exit does NOT fire, fail fires — head matched but subgoals failed downstream; (3) exit: unify and exit both fire — success; (4) not_accessed: predicate never reached. Standard Ochiai maps (direct_fail + subgoal_fail) queries as 'ef-covered' if accessed. Stratified SBFL adds separate suspiciousness scores for each fault type, giving higher weight to direct_fail events (more certain evidence of KB error at that predicate).\",\n      \"tie_breaking\": \"By predicate order or random; ties are common and usually resolved by listing all tied predicates for user inspection\"\n    },\n    \"swi_prolog_tracing\": {\n      \"recommended_approach\": \"meta-interpreter (Option B) — load via consult() from pyswip, record outcomes to Prolog global database, extract to Python via query(). This is more portable and reliable than the trace hook system for automated instrumentation.\",\n      \"hook_api_signature\": \"prolog_trace_interception(+Port, +Frame, +Choice, -Action)\",\n      \"hook_action_to_continue\": \"continue (equivalent to 'creep' in debugger — does not alter execution)\",\n      \"ports_full_list\": [\"call\", \"redo(PC)\", \"unify\", \"exit\", \"fail\", \"exception(Except)\", \"cut_call(PC)\", \"cut_exit(PC)\"],\n      \"ports_for_stratification\": {\n        \"direct_fault\": \"call fires AND unify does NOT fire — clause head does not unify with goal term\",\n        \"indirect_fault\": \"unify fires AND exit does NOT fire (fail fires next) — head matched but subgoals failed downstream\",\n        \"success\": \"unify fires AND exit fires — predicate fully proved\",\n        \"not_accessed\": \"neither call nor unify fires for this predicate in this query\"\n      },\n      \"frame_attributes\": {\n        \"goal\": \"Term of the goal associated with Frame — gives functor name and arguments\",\n        \"predicate_indicator\": \"<module>:<name>/<arity> — preferred over goal to avoid illegal terms\",\n        \"level\": \"Integer recursion depth of Frame (top-level = 0)\",\n        \"clause\": \"Reference to currently running clause\",\n        \"parent\": \"Reference to parent stack frame\"\n      },\n      \"pyswip_integration\": \"Use Prolog.consult('meta_interp.pl') to load the meta-interpreter, then Prolog.query('run_query(Goal, QueryId, Result)') to execute queries. Coverage events accumulate in the Prolog dynamic database and are extractable via Prolog.query('coverage(Pred, Event, QueryId)').\",\n      \"meta_interpreter_pattern\": \"% Instrumented vanilla meta-interpreter with outcome recording\\n:- dynamic coverage/3.  % coverage(Pred/Arity, Event, QueryId)\\n\\nprove(true, _) :- !.\\nprove((A, B), QId) :- !, prove(A, QId), prove(B, QId).\\nprove(Goal, QId) :-\\n    functor(Goal, Name, Arity),\\n    clause(Goal, Body),\\n    assertz(coverage(Name/Arity, unified, QId)),\\n    ( prove(Body, QId) ->\\n        assertz(coverage(Name/Arity, exit, QId))\\n    ;\\n        assertz(coverage(Name/Arity, subgoal_fail, QId)),\\n        fail\\n    ).\\nprove(Goal, QId) :-\\n    functor(Goal, Name, Arity),\\n    \\\\+ clause(Goal, _),\\n    assertz(coverage(Name/Arity, direct_fail, QId)),\\n    fail.\\n\\nrun_query(Goal, QId, Result) :-\\n    ( prove(Goal, QId) -> Result = proved ; Result = failed ).\",\n      \"decision\": \"Meta-interpreter (Option B) preferred because: (1) no need to arm/disarm SWI-Prolog debugger from Python; (2) portability across Prolog implementations; (3) simpler integration with pyswip's query() API; (4) full control over what constitutes a coverage event; (5) avoids complex interaction with prolog_trace_interception/4 mode switching.\"\n    },\n    \"logic_lm_prompting\": {\n      \"architecture\": \"Three-stage pipeline: (1) Problem Formulator (LLM + few-shot) translates NL to symbolic language; (2) Symbolic Reasoner (deterministic solver) performs inference; (3) Result Interpreter maps symbolic result back to NL answer.\",\n      \"few_shot_structure_folio\": \"Header: grammar definition with 8 FOL operator descriptions.   "summary": "This research artifact provides concrete, implementation-ready findings across 7 research areas required for the dual-signal SBFL pipeline:\n\n1. **Ochiai Formula**: Confirmed exact formula `ef / sqrt((ef+nf)*(ef+ep))` with variable definitions (ef=failed-test coverage, ep=passing-test coverage, nf=failed-test non-coverage, np not used).   "out_expected_files": {
    "output": "research_out.json"
  },
  "answer": "## Ochiai Formula and SBFL Coverage Matrix [1, 13]\n\nThe Ochiai suspiciousness formula is: `Ochiai(s) = ef(s) / sqrt((ef(s) + nf(s)) * (ef(s) + ep(s)))` [1]. The four coverage variables are: **ef** = number of *failed* test cases that execute element s; **ep** = number of *passing* test cases that execute element s; **nf** = number of *failed* test cases that do NOT execute s; **np** = number of *passing* test cases that do NOT execute s [1, 13]. Critically, **np is not used** in Ochiai (unlike Tarantula). The score range is [0,1] where 1 means maximum suspicion. For comparison, Tarantula(s) = (ef/totalfailed) / ((ef/totalfailed) + (ep/totalpassed)) [1].\n\nFor the Prolog context mapping: predicate clauses = program elements; oracle queries (NL premise set + NL question) = test cases; proof success matching gold label = test pass; proof failure or wrong label = test fail [4]. The stratified coverage extends the binary matrix: **direct_fail** (call port fires, unify does NOT) signals a head-matching failure; **subgoal_fail** (unify fires, exit does NOT) signals subgoal failures after successful head unification [2].\n\n## SWI-Prolog Tracing API [2, 3, 11]\n\nThe exact trace hook predicate is `prolog_trace_interception(+Port, +Frame, +Choice, -Action)` [2]. Port values relevant to stratified coverage are: `call` (predicate invoked), `unify` (neck instruction — head matching complete), `exit` (goal proved), `fail` (final failure) [2]. To continue without interference, return `Action = continue` [2]. Frame attributes accessible via `prolog_frame_attribute(Frame, Key, Value)` [3]: `goal` gives the goal term, `predicate_indicator` gives `<module>:<name>/<arity>` (preferred to avoid illegal terms), `level` gives recursion depth [3].\n\n**Recommended approach: pure Prolog meta-interpreter** loaded via pyswip's `consult()`, not trace hooks [2]. The meta-interpreter pattern records `coverage(Pred/Arity, Event, QueryId)` facts in the Prolog dynamic database. Events are: `unified` (head matched), `exit` (subgoals proved), `subgoal_fail` (head matched but subgoals failed), `direct_fail` (no matching clause head). Python extracts coverage via `list(prolog.query('coverage(Pred, Event, QId)'))` [4].\n\n## Logic-LM Prompting Format [4, 5, 6, 12]\n\nLogic-LM uses two symbolic formats depending on the reasoning type [4]: **FOLIO uses FOL format** with a 2-shot prompt: grammar header (8 FOL operator definitions) + two complete examples structured as `Predicates: / Premises: / Conclusion:` sections, with `:::` separating formulas from English glosses [5]. **ProofWriter uses LP format** with a 1-shot prompt: 4-step task description + one example structured as `Predicates: / Facts: / Rules: / Query:`, where predicates have bool parameters (`P($x, bool)`), facts use `P(Entity, True)` syntax, and rules use `>>>` arrow notation [6].\n\nPredicate naming: CamelCase for both formats (e.g., `ChoralConductor(x)`, `Dependent(x)`, `Love(x,y)`) [5]. Constants: lowercase atoms (`miroslav`, `rina`) or compound atoms (`year1946`) [5]. Self-refinement feeds solver **error messages** (not NL critique) back to the LLM iteratively until no errors or max revisions reached [4].\n\n## FOLIO Benchmark Protocol [7, 14]\n\nFOLIO contains 1,435 examples from 487 story sets, split as train=1001/val=203/test=226 [7]. Labels are True/False/Unknown [7]. **Evaluation metrics**: Accuracy for the logical reasoning task; **SynV** (syntactic validity — is the FOL formula parseable?) and **EAcc** (execution accuracy — does running the FOL through the inference engine produce the correct label?) for the NL-FOL translation task [7]. GPT-4 achieves ~93.9% SynV and ~63.8% EAcc with few-shot prompting [7]. The inference engine is a custom FOL prover (Appendix G of the paper). JSONL data format with fields: `story_id`, `premises` (NL list), `conclusion` (NL), `label`, `premises-FOL`, `conclusion-FOL` [7, 14]. Label distribution is not balanced — more True examples; models tend toward True predictions [7].\n\n## ProofWriter Benchmark Protocol [8]\n\nProofWriter provides five depth variants: D0 (0 hops), D1 (≤1), D2 (≤2), D3 (≤3), D5 (≤5 hops), each with 100k questions [8]. Two world assumption variants: CWA (True/False only) and OWA (True/False/Unknown) [8]. Logic-LM uses **OWA depth-5 test set, 600 randomly sampled examples** with balanced distribution (200 each PROVED/DISPROVED/UNKNOWN) [4]. LINC uses **OWA all-depths, 360 balanced samples** — 50 per depth (0-5), 120 per label, 20 per depth×label [9]. Data fields: `theory` (NL sentence list), `question` (NL conclusion), `answer`, `proof` (structured tree) [8]. Under CWA, Prolog's `\\+` maps cleanly; under OWA, a three-way classifier is needed [8].\n\n## Self-Refine Baseline [10]\n\nSelf-Refine uses three prompts: `pgen` (initial generation), `pfb` (feedback), `prefine` (refinement) [10]. Algorithm: generate y0, then iteratively: fb = M(pfb||x||y), if stop: break, else y' = M(prefine||x||y0||fb0||...||y||fb) [10]. Stopping: fixed max iterations OR model self-determines no further refinement needed [10]. Feedback is **global NL critique** (actionable, specific — identifies concrete phrases to change) [10]. For Prolog KB context, Self-Refine would provide: 'Query Q fails; predicate P appears incorrect' — NOT ranked suspiciousness scores. This is the key differentiator: SBFL provides ranked per-predicate numeric scores enabling targeted repair, while Self-Refine provides unstructured holistic NL critique requiring the LLM to self-localize the error.\n\n## LINC Baseline [9]\n\nLINC uses **8-shot in-context learning** with examples hand-picked from the FOLIO training set [9]. The same 8 examples are used for both FOLIO and ProofWriter evaluation [9]. FOL representation uses **Prover9 syntax** (NOT Prolog): `all x. (rectangle(x) -> foursides(x))` with lowercase predicates and variables, XML-style `<PREMISE>` / `<CONCLUSION>` tags [9]. The theorem prover is Prover9 (external FOL prover), NOT SWI-Prolog [9]. LINC samples N translations from the LLM, runs each through Prover9, filters syntax errors, and takes majority vote [9]. Failure modes: L1 (missing implicit commonsense), L2 (NL nuance not capturable in FOL), L3 (predicate naming inconsistencies across premises) [9]. Performance: GPT-4+LINC achieves 72.5% on FOLIO and ~92% on ProofWriter [9].",

Frame attributes accessible via `prolog_frame_attribute(Frame, Key, Value)` [3]: `goal` gives the goal term, `predicate_indicator` gives `<module>:<name>/<arity>` (preferred to avoid illegal terms), `level` gives recursion depth [3].\\n\\n**Recommended approach: pure Prolog meta-interpreter** loaded via pyswip's `consult()`, not trace hooks [2]. The meta-interpreter pattern records `coverage(Pred/Arity, Event, QueryId)` facts in the Prolog dynamic database. Events are: `unified` (head matched), `exit` (subgoals proved), `subgoal_fail` (head matched but subgoals failed), `direct_fail` (no matching clause head). Python extracts coverage via `list(prolog.query('coverage(Pred, Event, QId)'))` [4].\\n\\n## Logic-LM Prompting Format [4, 5, 6, 12]\\n\\nLogic-LM uses two symbolic formats depending on the reasoning type [4]: **FOLIO uses FOL format** with a 2-shot prompt: grammar header (8 FOL operator definitions) + two complete examples structured as `Predicates: / Premises: / Conclusion:` sections, with `:::` separating formulas from English glosses [5]. **ProofWriter uses LP format** with a 1-shot prompt: 4-step task description + one example structured as `Predicates: / Facts: / Rules: / Query:`, where predicates have bool parameters (`P($x, bool)`), facts use `P(Entity, True)` syntax, and rules use `>>>` arrow notation [6].\\n\\nPredicate naming: CamelCase for both formats (e.g., `ChoralConductor(x)`, `Dependent(x)`, `Love(x,y)`) [5]. Constants: lowercase atoms (`miroslav`, `rina`) or compound atoms (`year1946`) [5]. Self-refinement feeds solver **error messages** (not NL critique) back to the LLM iteratively until no errors or max revisions reached [4].\\n\\n## FOLIO Benchmark Protocol [7, 14]\\n\\nFOLIO contains 1,435 examples from 487 story sets, split as train=1001/val=203/test=226 [7]. Labels are True/False/Unknown [7]. **Evaluation metrics**: Accuracy for the logical reasoning task; **SynV** (syntactic validity — is the FOL formula parseable?) and **EAcc** (execution accuracy — does running the FOL through the inference engine produce the correct label?) for the NL-FOL translation task [7]. GPT-4 achieves ~93.9% SynV and ~63.8% EAcc with few-shot prompting [7]. The inference engine is a custom FOL prover (Appendix G of the paper). JSONL data format with fields: `story_id`, `premises` (NL list), `conclusion` (NL), `label`, `premises-FOL`, `conclusion-FOL` [7, 14]. Label distribution is not balanced — more True examples; models tend toward True predictions [7].\\n\\n## ProofWriter Benchmark Protocol [8]\\n\\nProofWriter provides five depth variants: D0 (0 hops), D1 (≤1), D2 (≤2), D3 (≤3), D5 (≤5 hops), each with 100k questions [8]. Two world assumption variants: CWA (True/False only) and OWA (True/False/Unknown) [8]. Logic-LM uses **OWA depth-5 test set, 600 randomly sampled examples** with balanced distribution (200 each PROVED/DISPROVED/UNKNOWN) [4]. LINC uses **OWA all-depths, 360 balanced samples** — 50 per depth (0-5), 120 per label, 20 per depth×label [9]. Data fields: `theory` (NL sentence list), `question` (NL conclusion), `answer`, `proof` (structured tree) [8]. Under CWA, Prolog's `\\\\+` maps cleanly; under OWA, a three-way classifier is needed [8].\\n\\n## Self-Refine Baseline [10]\\n\\nSelf-Refine uses three prompts: `pgen` (initial generation), `pfb` (feedback), `prefine` (refinement) [10]. Algorithm: generate y0, then iteratively: fb = M(pfb||x||y), if stop: break, else y' = M(prefine||x||y0||fb0||...||y||fb) [10]. Stopping: fixed max iterations OR model self-determines no further refinement needed [10]. Feedback is **global NL critique** (actionable, specific — identifies concrete phrases to change) [10]. For Prolog KB context, Self-Refine would provide: 'Query Q fails; predicate P appears incorrect' — NOT ranked suspiciousness scores. This is the key differentiator: SBFL provides ranked per-predicate numeric scores enabling targeted repair, while Self-Refine provides unstructured holistic NL critique requiring the LLM to self-localize the error.\\n\\n## LINC Baseline [9]\\n\\nLINC uses **8-shot in-context learning** with examples hand-picked from the FOLIO training set [9]. The same 8 examples are used for both FOLIO and ProofWriter evaluation [9]. FOL representation uses **Prover9 syntax** (NOT Prolog): `all x. (rectangle(x) -> foursides(x))` with lowercase predicates and variables, XML-style `<PREMISE>` / `<CONCLUSION>` tags [9]. The theorem prover is Prover9 (external FOL prover), NOT SWI-Prolog [9]. LINC samples N translations from the LLM, runs each through Prover9, filters syntax errors, and takes majority vote [9]. Failure modes: L1 (missing implicit commonsense), L2 (NL nuance not capturable in FOL), L3 (predicate naming inconsistencies across premises) [9]. Performance: GPT-4+LINC achieves 72.5% on FOLIO and ~92% on ProofWriter [9].\",\n  \"sources\": [\n    {\n      \"index\": 1,\n      \"url\": \"https://arxiv.org/pdf/1803.09939\",\n      \"title\": \"An Empirical Study of Fault Localization Families and Their Combinations (Zou et al., 2019)\",\n      \"summary\": \"Confirmed exact Ochiai formula: ef/sqrt((ef+nf)*(ef+ep)). Defined all four SBFL coverage matrix variables. Compared Ochiai with DStar and Tarantula. Key SBFL empirical reference.\"\n    },\n    {\n      \"index\": 2,\n      \"url\": \"https://www.swi-prolog.org/pldoc/man?predicate=prolog_trace_interception%2F4\",\n      \"title\": \"SWI-Prolog prolog_trace_interception/4 Official Documentation\",\n      \"summary\": \"Complete predicate signature, all port types (call, redo, unify, exit, fail, exception, cut_call, cut_exit), all action values (continue, nodebug, abort, fail, skip, etc.), and example code for recording trace events.\"\n    },\n    {\n      \"index\": 3,\n      \"url\": \"https://www.swi-prolog.org/pldoc/man?predicate=prolog_frame_attribute%2F3\",\n      \"title\": \"SWI-Prolog prolog_frame_attribute/3 Official Documentation\",\n      \"summary\": \"All frame attribute keys: goal, predicate_indicator, level, clause, parent, argument(N). ### [96] ASSISTANT · 2026-06-07 05:07:34 UTC

```
The research is complete. Here's a summary of what was found and documented:

**Key findings across all 7 research steps:**

1. **Ochiai formula** [1, 13]: Exact formula `ef / sqrt((ef+nf)*(ef+ep))` confirmed. np not used. Prolog mapping: predicates as elements, oracle queries as tests. Stratified coverage adds three event types (direct_fail, subgoal_fail, success) via SLD port monitoring.

2. **SWI-Prolog tracing** [2, 3]: Full `prolog_trace_interception/4` API documented. **Recommended: meta-interpreter approach** over trace hooks — simpler pyswip integration, no debugger mode management. Concrete code pattern provided for recording unification outcomes.

3. **Logic-LM prompting** [4, 5, 6]: Actual prompt files retrieved from GitHub. FOLIO uses 2-shot FOL format (Unicode, CamelCase, `:::` glosses). ProofWriter uses 1-shot LP format (bool params, `>>>` syntax). Self-refinement uses solver *error messages*, not NL critique.

4. **FOLIO benchmark** [7]: train=1001/val=203/test=226; True/False/Unknown; metrics: Accuracy + SynV (~93.9%) + EAcc (~63.8%); custom FOL inference engine; JSONL format.

5. **ProofWriter benchmark** [8]: D0-D5 variants (100k each), OWA recommended (three-label schema), Logic-LM: 600 balanced OWA-D5 samples, LINC: 360 balanced samples across depths.

6. **Self-Refine** [10]: Three-prompt structure; global NL critique (holistic) vs. SBFL's ranked per-predicate numeric scores (targeted).

7. **LINC** [9]: 8-shot ICL, Prover9 FOL syntax (not Prolog), majority voting. Three failure modes. 72.5% on FOLIO, ~92% on ProofWriter with GPT-4.
```

{
  "title": "SBFL Ochiai Formula, SWI-Prolog Tracing API, Logic-LM NL-to-FOL Prompting Format, FOLIO and ProofWriter Benchmark Schemas for Dual-Signal Fault Localization Pipeline",
  "summary": "Comprehensive survey covering: (1) Ochiai SBFL formula ef/sqrt((ef+nf)*(ef+ep)) with Prolog predicate-to-coverage-matrix mapping and stratified direct/indirect fault classification; (2) SWI-Prolog prolog_trace_interception/4 and prolog_frame_attribute/3 APIs, with recommendation to use a pure Prolog meta-interpreter via pyswip for portable SLD coverage recording; (3) Logic-LM's actual few-shot prompt format for FOLIO (2-shot FOL with Unicode symbols and ::: glosses) and ProofWriter (1-shot LP with bool params and >>> rule syntax), plus self-refinement using solver error messages; (4) FOLIO benchmark: 1435 examples, train=1001/val=203/test=226, True/False/Unknown labels, Accuracy + SynV + EAcc metrics, custom FOL inference engine, JSONL format; (5) ProofWriter: D0-D5 depth variants (100k each), OWA recommended (three-label schema), Logic-LM uses 600 balanced OWA-D5 samples; (6) Self-Refine three-prompt structure with global NL critique vs. SBFL ranked scores; (7) LINC: 8-shot ICL, Prover9 FOL syntax (not Prolog), majority voting, three failure modes.",
  "answer": "## Ochiai Formula and SBFL Coverage Matrix\n\nThe Ochiai suspiciousness formula is: Ochiai(s) = ef(s) / sqrt((ef(s) + nf(s)) * (ef(s) + ep(s))) [1, 13]. The four coverage variables are: ef = number of failed test cases that execute element s; ep = number of passing test cases that execute element s; nf = number of failed test cases that do NOT execute s; np = number of passing test cases that do NOT execute s [1, 13]. Critically, np is not used in Ochiai (unlike Tarantula). The score range is [0,1] where 1 means maximum suspicion. For comparison, Tarantula(s) = (ef/totalfailed) / ((ef/totalfailed) + (ep/totalpassed)) [1].\n\nFor the Prolog context mapping: predicate clauses are program elements; oracle queries (NL premise set + NL question) are test cases; proof success matching gold label = test pass; proof failure or wrong label = test fail [4]. Stratified coverage extends the binary matrix with three event types: direct_fail (call port fires, unify does NOT — head mismatch); subgoal_fail (unify fires, exit does NOT — head matched but subgoals failed); success (both unify and exit fire) [2].\n\n## SWI-Prolog Tracing API\n\nThe exact trace hook predicate is prolog_trace_interception(+Port, +Frame, +Choice, -Action) [2]. Port values relevant to stratified coverage are: call (predicate invoked), unify (neck instruction — head matching complete), exit (goal proved), fail (final failure) [2]. To continue without interference, return Action = continue [2]. Frame attributes accessible via prolog_frame_attribute(Frame, Key, Value) [3]: goal gives the goal term, predicate_indicator gives module:name/arity (preferred to avoid illegal terms), level gives recursion depth [3].\n\nRecommended approach: pure Prolog meta-interpreter loaded via pyswip's consult(), not trace hooks [2, 11]. The meta-interpreter records coverage(Pred/Arity, Event, QueryId) facts in the Prolog dynamic database. Events: unified (head matched), exit (subgoals proved), subgoal_fail, direct_fail. Python extracts coverage via list(prolog.query('coverage(Pred, Event, QId)')) [4]. The meta-interpreter pattern is: prove(true,_):-!. prove((A,B),Q):-!,prove(A,Q),prove(B,Q). prove(Goal,Q):- clause(Goal,Body), assertz(coverage(Name/Arity,unified,Q)), (prove(Body,Q) -> assertz(coverage(Name/Arity,exit,Q)) ; assertz(coverage(Name/Arity,subgoal_fail,Q)), fail). prove(Goal,Q):- \\+clause(Goal,_), assertz(coverage(Name/Arity,direct_fail,Q)), fail. [2, 11]\n\n## Logic-LM Prompting Format\n\nLogic-LM uses a three-stage pipeline: Problem Formulator (LLM + few-shot translates NL to symbolic), Symbolic Reasoner (deterministic solver), Result Interpreter [4]. Two symbolic formats are used depending on the dataset [4]: FOLIO uses a 2-shot FOL format with a grammar header (8 FOL operator definitions using Unicode symbols) and examples structured as Predicates / Premises / Conclusion sections with ::: separating formulas from English glosses [5]. ProofWriter uses a 1-shot LP format with a 4-step task description and examples structured as Predicates (bool params) / Facts / Rules (>>> syntax) / Query sections [6].\n\nPredicate naming: CamelCase for both formats (e.g., ChoralConductor(x), Dependent(x), Love(x,y)) [5]. Constants are lowercase atoms (miroslav, rina) or compound atoms (year1946) [5]. Logic-LM's self-refinement feeds solver error messages (NOT natural language critique) back to the LLM iteratively until no errors or max revisions reached [4]. The ProofWriter evaluation uses OWA depth-5 subset, randomly sampling 600 examples from the test set with balanced label distribution (200 each PROVED/DISPROVED/UNKNOWN) [4].\n\n## FOLIO Benchmark Protocol\n\nFOLIO contains 1,435 examples from 487 story sets, split as train=1001 / val=203 / test=226 [7]. Labels are True / False / Unknown [7]. Evaluation metrics: Accuracy for the logical reasoning task; SynV (syntactic validity — is the FOL formula parseable by the inference engine? GPT-4 achieves ~93.9% with few-shot) and EAcc (execution accuracy — does running the FOL through the inference engine produce the correct label? GPT-4 achieves ~63.8% with few-shot) for the NL-FOL translation task [7]. The inference engine is a custom FOL prover (Appendix G of the FOLIO paper) [7]. JSONL data format with fields: story_id, premises (NL list), conclusion (NL string), label, premises-FOL (FOL formula list), conclusion-FOL (FOL formula string) [7, 14]. Label distribution is not balanced — more True examples; models tend toward True predictions [7]. LINC uses the validation set with 182 examples (removing 22 with annotation errors) [9]. Expert annotators achieve 95.98% accuracy on FOLIO, non-experts achieve 61.82%, and GPT-4 falls ~31.82 percentage points below experts [7].\n\n## ProofWriter Benchmark Protocol\n\nProofWriter provides five depth variants: D0 (0 hops), D1 (at most 1 hop), D2 (at most 2 hops), D3 (at most 3 hops), D5 (at most 5 hops), each with 100k questions [8]. Two world assumption variants exist: CWA (Closed-World Assumption, labels True/False only) and OWA (Open-World Assumption, labels True/False/Unknown) [8]. Logic-LM uses OWA depth-5 test set with 600 randomly sampled examples, balanced across labels [4]. LINC uses OWA all-depths with 360 balanced samples: 50 per depth (0-5), 120 per label (True/False/Uncertain), 20 per depth×label combination [9]. Data fields per example: theory (list of NL sentences = facts + rules), question (NL conclusion to evaluate), answer (True/False/Unknown), proof (structured proof tree with intermediate steps) [8]. Under CWA, Prolog's \\+ (negation as failure) maps cleanly to ProofWriter semantics; under OWA, a three-way classifier is needed [8].\n\n## Self-Refine Baseline\n\nSelf-Refine uses three prompts: pgen (initial generation — few-shot examples of input→output), pfb (feedback — few-shot examples of input+output→feedback with actionable NL critique), and prefine (refinement — full history fed back) [10]. The algorithm: y0 = M(pgen||x); then iterate: fb = M(pfb||x||y), if stop: break, else y' = M(prefine||x||y0||fb0||...||y||fb) [10]. Stopping conditions: fixed maximum iterations OR model self-determines no further refinement needed [10]. Feedback is a global NL critique — actionable and specific, identifying concrete phrases to change [10]. Self-Refine improves outputs by ~20% absolute on average across 7 tasks [10]. The key structural differentiator from SBFL: Self-Refine gives unstructured holistic NL critique requiring the LLM to self-localize errors, while SBFL provides ranked per-predicate numeric suspiciousness scores enabling targeted repair [10].\n\n## LINC Baseline\n\nLINC uses 8-shot in-context learning with examples hand-picked from the FOLIO training set, using the same 8 examples for both FOLIO and ProofWriter evaluation [9]. The FOL representation uses Prover9 syntax (NOT Prolog LP syntax): universal quantification as 'all x. (p(x) -> q(x))', existential as 'exists x. (p(x))', with XML-style PREMISE and CONCLUSION tags wrapping each sentence [9]. The theorem prover is Prover9 (external FOL prover, not SWI-Prolog) [9]. LINC samples N translations from the LLM, runs each through Prover9, filters syntax errors, and takes majority vote on remaining valid outputs [9]. Three documented failure modes without feedback: L1 (FOL misses implicit commonsense not stated in premises), L2 (natural language nuance not capturable in first-order logic), L3 (predicate naming inconsistencies across premises, e.g., foursides vs. foursidedthings) [9]. Performance: GPT-4+LINC achieves 72.5% on FOLIO and ~92% on ProofWriter [9]. StarCoder+15.5B+LINC outperforms GPT-4+CoT on ProofWriter by 10% absolute [9].",
